So those with braces, retainers, or just like water irrigator's listen up.<br /><br />Waterpik:<br />I currently have (throwing out soon) the waterpik that you plug into the wall with the full tank. This should be a reference point for those reading, as I did not have the portable waterpik, because it didn't produce the same amount of power.<br /><br />Aspects the TolietTree Irrigator produces, compared to Waterpik:<br />1. Waterpik's system is difficult to use on maximum power, without creating a flooding water mess of your sink. And for those of you who recently purchased a waterpik, you might want to know that the handle that holds your device to the water tank, is going to brake off. Happens everytime, with all of my friends too, and it isn't because we are rough. Waterpik just uses cheap plastic.<br /><br />2. Nicer design.<br />This may seem like a vanity point, but it isn't. The materials this water irrigator is made from, isn't as cheap as the waterpik, and doesn't mold. Yep, that's right mold. Unless you thoroughly wash your waterpik out once a week, even if you aren't using it for a while, it will form mold in the top pockets of the lid that covers the tank. Think I'm lying? Try it out, it's disgusting!<br /><br />3. Better choices for irrigation.<br />This device has three motor options, a regular high function irrigation, I'd compare to a 9 on the waterpik, and then a pulse setting, which is perfect for those of you whom have braces, and need to work around the brackets, and then the third setting which is a soft, which I'd say would be meant more for newbies in the first week, and even those with retainers. It always stays in my bathroom right? Wrong. The one time you need to use it for travel, or need to move, you'll know what I'm talking about the hard way. They have the same amount of power regardless of what the box tells you. I'v used both back to back, and they are putting out the exact same amount of power.<br /><br />Tips that might make you puzzled when the ToiletTree water irrigator arrives:<br /><br />1. The fill tank is very small. I'm a traveller, and because of this, I have a portable iron. With the portable iron, came a small cup, that I could use to fill it with water, and I use that to fill this. You can either go the same route and pour water slowly from a cup, as I would not suggest you use hardwater from a tap, or you can remove the tank from the drevice, and then snap it back into place when full.<br /><br />2. It does take time to charge, and you can't use it whilst on the charger. I believe this is a good safety feature, as the water if being used whilst charging would have the potential to run down to the charge plug, which is located in the front of the device.<br /><br />3. It comes with a replacement head, so use it. Don't necessarily use one until you cannot any longer and then throw it away to use the other.
